<div id="review_1961035193" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1961035193" />
    <a title="Ahmed  Ejaz" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/53694260-ahmed-ejaz"><img alt="Ahmed  Ejaz" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598778737p2/53694260.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1961035193?book_show_action=true">Apr 05, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ahmed  Ejaz" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ahmed  Ejaz" href="/user/show/53694260-ahmed-ejaz">Ahmed  Ejaz</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/30831912-norse-mythology">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53694260-ahmed-ejaz?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53694260-ahmed-ejaz?shelf=full-lengths">full-lengths</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1961035193" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15512358606095658675"><b>**Spoiler Free Review**</b><br/><blockquote> <b><i> There is no glory without danger</i></b></blockquote><i> Before beginning the review, I clear out that I read this book as a fictional work not as the work which I believe can be/is true. I am telling you because this book was getting little serious about narrating these myths. Like trying to make us believe these are real facts. </i> <br/>Now, the actual review: <br/>This book is the re-writing of Norse Mythology. Author doesn't exaggerate the facts. He simply re-writes some of the popular myths in pretty s</span>
  <span id="freeText15512358606095658675" style="display:none"><b>**Spoiler Free Review**</b><br /><blockquote> <b><i> There is no glory without danger</i></b></blockquote><i> Before beginning the review, I clear out that I read this book as a fictional work not as the work which I believe can be/is true. I am telling you because this book was getting little serious about narrating these myths. Like trying to make us believe these are real facts. </i> <br />Now, the actual review: <br />This book is the re-writing of Norse Mythology. Author doesn't exaggerate the facts. He simply re-writes some of the popular myths in pretty straight-forward way. I really liked the writing style. <br />Most of the myths are about Odin, Thor and Loki. <br /><br />In the whole fifteen myths, I just loved four:<br />=&gt; The Children of Loki<br />=&gt;Freya's Unusual Wedding <br />[this is hilarious]<br />=&gt;Thor's Journey to the Land's of Giants <br />[this myth has some great universal truths]<br />=&gt; The Treasures of gods <br />[if you wanna know how Thor got his Hammer, read it]<br /><br />These are those which I enjoyed the most. Other than these were just fine. Some of them I liked as a fiction. Some of them I didn't even like as a fiction. <br /><br />I liked Loki. He was clever. Evil. Cause of every bad deed. But he was little good too. I couldn't decide whether he was completely good or completely bad. Thor was also good. I liked reading his myths too. I couldn't like Odin that much. He was just fine.<br /><br />After reading this book, I wouldn't recommend this book to children. Even though this book is totally fine for them. But still I won't be recommending this to them. I hope some of you have gotten an idea why I am saying this. Believe me this book is totally fine for them. But I am not feeling that they should read this book. Of course when they will have grown-up then there is no harm.<br /><br />Or the most important thing I almost forgot to tell you that this was my first Mythology reading. I thought these were just like our regular fantasy genre. But now I think that there is a great joy in reading myths as a part of books' plot. Like Rick Reordan's books. Rather than reading the original myths. Don't get me wrong, please!<br /><br />Nevertheless, this book is good. Highly recommended for those who love reading original myths. But not for children until their mature age.<br /><br /><b>☆☆3.5 Stars☆☆<br /><blockquote> <b> <i> When something goes wrong, the first thing I always think is, it is Loki’s fault. It saves a lot of time </i></b>-- Thor</blockquote></b><br />April 5, 2017</span>
  <a data-text-id="15512358606095658675" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_3158365985" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3158365985" />
    <a title="Peter" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10477405-peter"><img alt="Peter" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1340652114p2/10477405.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3158365985?book_show_action=true">Jan 24, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Peter" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Peter" href="/user/show/10477405-peter">Peter</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10477405-peter?shelf=horror">horror</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3158365985" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10591573818532851362">If you never read Northern mythologies before or only heard about the Northern Pantheon by a Marvel movie (the author refers to them in his introduction) this is certainly the book to get a good entry into that world. Neil Gaiman professionally introduces in a modern and fluent narrative what it is about and who the main players are. You come to know why Thor once dressed up as a woman, learn where poetry does come from and wonder about the timeless wisdom that no one can beat old age. Packed ch</span>
  <span id="freeText10591573818532851362" style="display:none">If you never read Northern mythologies before or only heard about the Northern Pantheon by a Marvel movie (the author refers to them in his introduction) this is certainly the book to get a good entry into that world. Neil Gaiman professionally introduces in a modern and fluent narrative what it is about and who the main players are. You come to know why Thor once dressed up as a woman, learn where poetry does come from and wonder about the timeless wisdom that no one can beat old age. Packed chapters tell of Thor, Thyr, Odin, Loki and their adventures. You see how the world was structured back then and what was good or evil. My favourites were the death of Balder, the last days of Loki and the apocalyptic Ragnarok, the final destiny and destruction of the Gods. The end of the old times. Well, so far so good. Was there anything new to Northern Mythology as I read it way back in my childhood and youth? Unfortunately not too much. Certainly a good book if you want to have some more background to a Marvel movie or comic but not sufficient for the experienced Mythologist. It's easy to read though and brought back some memories of the old stories. A good basic work, a fine cover and a quick read. But don't expect any new aspects. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10591573818532851362" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2178097576" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2178097576" />
    <a title="Miranda Reads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads"><img alt="Miranda Reads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592243041p2/71848701.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2178097576?book_show_action=true">Dec 01, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Miranda Reads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Miranda Reads" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads">Miranda Reads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9780062663641" href="/book/show/30988092-norse-mythology">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2178097576" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5786559658990553356"><blockquote>
  <i>“Because,” said Thor, “when something goes wrong, the first thing I always think is, it is Loki’s fault. It saves a lot of time.” </i>
</blockquote>This is my first comprehensive book on Norse Mythology and I was not a huge fan. <b>Everything seems too disconnected. </b> The Gods actions, their reactions, their punishments all don't seem to fit. There wasn't fluidity between one legend and the next - it <b>felt like a bunch of disjointed vignettes</b> featuring the same characters.<br/><br/>But, considering most of my knowledge is b</span>
  <span id="freeText5786559658990553356" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>“Because,” said Thor, “when something goes wrong, the first thing I always think is, it is Loki’s fault. It saves a lot of time.” </i>
</blockquote>This is my first comprehensive book on Norse Mythology and I was not a huge fan. <b>Everything seems too disconnected. </b> The Gods actions, their reactions, their punishments all don't seem to fit. There wasn't fluidity between one legend and the next - it <b>felt like a bunch of disjointed vignettes</b> featuring the same characters.<br /><br />But, considering most of my knowledge is based on Marvel movies, I can't tell if bits of the stories are being <b>left out in this rendition, </b> if it's Gaiman's particular style or if this is <b>just how the myths are told.</b> If they are anything like Greek myths, I think it could be just due to the oral traditions being scattered and warped every time they're told.<br /><br />I did enjoy Gaiman's style of writing. Yes, these tales are ancient but they didn't <i>quite</i> feel so old. Gaiman inserts humor through the word-choice that while likely not a literal translation, it certainly made for better listening.<blockquote>
  <i>I’m not happy about any of this,” said Thor. “I’m going to kill somebody soon, just to relieve the tension. You’ll see.</i>
</blockquote>There's such a <b>steep curve for keeping track of the people and things.</b> I kept having to rewind my audiobook to figure out what I missed. Everything, right down to the cauldrons and the hammers have difficult names and sometimes multiple names. However, listening to the audiobook did make it slightly easier to handle all of those names. <blockquote>
  <i>Of course it was Loki. It's always Loki.</i>
</blockquote><b>Audiobook Comments</b><br />Read by the author (a definitely plus)...and reading all of those crazy names was difficult but listening to them being said was significantly better for keeping track.<br /><br /><a href="http://bit.ly/33ii2CT" rel="nofollow noopener">YouTube</a> | <a href="http://www.mirandareads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/miranda.reads/?hl=en" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/Miranda_Reads" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | Snapchat @miranda.reads <br /><br />Happy Reading!</span>
  <a data-text-id="5786559658990553356" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="J.L.   Sutton" class="user" itemprop="url" name="J.L.   Sutton" href="/user/show/3675162-j-l-sutton">J.L.   Sutton</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2722719248" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16192199466078895571">If you want to read myths and stories about the gods of Valhalla, Neil Gaiman's Norse Mythology is quick, accessible and an entertaining way to delve into the subject. Some of the tales were short and fragmented, but that allows the reader to see the difference between the source material and the way these legends have evolved in the modern day. What really makes this compelling is the fact that Gaiman is such a great storyteller himself. The gods are no longer characters in a superhero universe</span>
  <span id="freeText16192199466078895571" style="display:none">If you want to read myths and stories about the gods of Valhalla, Neil Gaiman's Norse Mythology is quick, accessible and an entertaining way to delve into the subject. Some of the tales were short and fragmented, but that allows the reader to see the difference between the source material and the way these legends have evolved in the modern day. What really makes this compelling is the fact that Gaiman is such a great storyteller himself. The gods are no longer characters in a superhero universe. They belong to their own time and distinct place. Without changing the essential stories, Gaiman brings life to them. 4.5 stars. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16192199466078895571" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1929091012" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1929091012" />
    <a title="Seemita" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/34622220-seemita"><img alt="Seemita" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473185997p2/34622220.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1929091012?book_show_action=true">Mar 15, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Seemita" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Seemita" href="/user/show/34622220-seemita">Seemita</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781408890462" href="/book/show/33817397-norse-mythology">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34622220-seemita?shelf=culture">culture</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34622220-seemita?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34622220-seemita?shelf=nordic">nordic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34622220-seemita?shelf=anthology-collection">anthology-collection</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34622220-seemita?shelf=mythology">mythology</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34622220-seemita?shelf=religion">religion</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1929091012" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9025668279420369605"><i>[Originally appeared here: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://timesofindia.indiatimes.com/life-style/books/features/review-norse-mythology/articleshow/57734593.cms'>http://timesofindia.indiatimes.com/li...</a>]</i><br/><br/>Of all the fiction in this world, I find the ones rooted in mythology the most enticing; not because there is an element of otherworldly magic in them but because somewhere deep down, a bewitching veil of truth hovers above them. The characters we read of, the prowess we fall to, the betrayals we appall at and the spells we dive in, have all a debatable root which almost like our very own <i>
  <a href='https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Samudra_manthan' rel='nofollow noopener'>samudra manthan</a>
</i> of the Hindu mytholo</span>
  <span id="freeText9025668279420369605" style="display:none"><i>[Originally appeared here: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://timesofindia.indiatimes.com/life-style/books/features/review-norse-mythology/articleshow/57734593.cms">http://timesofindia.indiatimes.com/li...</a>]</i><br><br>Of all the fiction in this world, I find the ones rooted in mythology the most enticing; not because there is an element of otherworldly magic in them but because somewhere deep down, a bewitching veil of truth hovers above them. The characters we read of, the prowess we fall to, the betrayals we appall at and the spells we dive in, have all a debatable root which almost like our very own <i>
  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Samudra_manthan" rel="nofollow noopener">samudra manthan</a>
</i> of the Hindu mythology, can be twisted this way or that. As most myths are made lesser of primary evidence and more of a secondary interpretation, there is a hidden little room of sorts from where you can see as far as you can, like Heimdall in this book. He is a kind of parallel to Mahabharata’s <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sanjaya" rel="nofollow noopener">Sanjaya</a>.<br><br>Neil Gaiman takes the essence of Norse mythology and spins a riveting web around it. Although he makes it clear in the beginning that this book will focus on the three towering characters of Odin, the all-father of gods, Thor, Odin’s powerful son and Loki, Odin’s shrewd, evil blood-brother (and eventual enemy), the chapters easily transcend the trio and throw open an enchanted window to the Germanic myths. Chronicling the journey right from the beginning when nothing existed and going all the way to Ragnarok, the apocalyptic war that wiped the gods and the giants, Gaiman deploys an easy and engaging language to retell the myths that remain fraught with magic, power, bonds, guilt, murder, betrayal, repentance, revenge and redemption. I chuckled at the story where Thor and his two companions are put to a series of illusory tests by a giant who didn’t want his kingdom to be usurped by the mighty Thor. I felt sombre at the unfortunate fate that was handed over to the Hel, Fenrir and Jörmungandr, the children of Loki from a giantess, just because they didn’t resemble the gods. I read with palpable excitement the battle of skills when the two most accomplished dwarfs, the craftsmen of the Norse world, were pitted against each other to create the most unique gifts for the gods. Mjölnir, the heroic hammer of Thor, was an outcome of this competition.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1490074285i/22277972._SX540_.jpg" width="700" height="350" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>For most parts, the chapters were taut and action-oriented. Crisp and to the point, the narrative had a very clear agenda of telling the myths the way they were documented to be told. However, for the keen eyes who look out for detailed landscape and an aura of environment that inevitably leave a mark on the characters and their becoming with the passage of time, there may be something amiss. Questions of morality and immorality, mortality and immortality, lay suspended without direction. Now, perhaps, the objective of this book was to stuff in as many incidents as possible into the terse 300 pages, effectively closing the alternative of detailed painting and reflecting. However, Gaiman’s version remains faithful to the original and one may ditch the expansive road in the favour of a vertiginous fall.<br><br>----<br><br><i>
  <a href="https://fleetingbrook.wordpress.com/2017/03/29/book-review-norse-mythology-by-neil-gaiman-2017/" rel="nofollow noopener">Also on my blog.</a>
</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="9025668279420369605" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1835830539" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1835830539" />
    <a title="Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes"><img alt="Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598297811p2/1452829.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1835830539?book_show_action=true">Feb 09, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~" href="/user/show/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes">Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780393609097" href="/book/show/30809689-norse-mythology">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes?shelf=3-star">3-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes?shelf=year-2017">year-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1835830539" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9744822154489717995">I do not have a strong knowledge of <u>any</u> mythology as a general rule. It's something I've been wanting to remedy for a while, but it's a <i>vast</i> subject.<br/><br/>I've known for a while that Gaiman was working on <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30809689.Norse_Mythology' title='Norse Mythology by Neil Gaiman' rel='nofollow noopener'>Norse Mythology</a> (for almost 8 years wowza!), and that many of his stories and characters take inspiration from the Norse tales. So naturally, I pre-ordered this one.<br/><br/>I did enjoy this. It's a selection of tales, mostly focusing on Odin, Loki, and Thor, that all lead up to Ragnarok, the end of the world</span>
  <span id="freeText9744822154489717995" style="display:none">I do not have a strong knowledge of <u>any</u> mythology as a general rule. It's something I've been wanting to remedy for a while, but it's a <i>vast</i> subject.<br /><br />I've known for a while that Gaiman was working on <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30809689.Norse_Mythology" title="Norse Mythology by Neil Gaiman" rel="nofollow noopener">Norse Mythology</a> (for almost 8 years wowza!), and that many of his stories and characters take inspiration from the Norse tales. So naturally, I pre-ordered this one.<br /><br />I did enjoy this. It's a selection of tales, mostly focusing on Odin, Loki, and Thor, that all lead up to Ragnarok, the end of the world. It's a quick read, and decently accurate. Gaiman retold these stories in an interesting way, in layman's terms, and definitely taught me a couple things I did not know. <br /><br />I think this book accomplished what it set out to accomplish, but I guess I was looking for a little <b>more.</b> I haven't read scores of mythology books in order to know how this holds up against other existing works, but I stayed present more for Gaiman's <u>brilliant writing style</u> than for the actual stories he chose to retell.<br /><br />Throughout the book I saw glimpses of some characters I would've liked to hear more about, such as Fenrir, Loki's wolf son. Perhaps substantial material on these gods does not exist, but they caught my attention and I definitely wanted to explore more of their story. But as I mentioned earlier, a large portion of the focus was on Loki and Thor.<br /><br /><b>I must say though Loki is a very interesting dude... maybe I'm just ignorant but I didn't realize he is literally at the heart of every problem.</b><br /><br />From his author's note, I'm to understand that Gaiman would've liked to focus on some lesser known Gods, but that there simply is not enough source material to accurately and effectively retell their tales. While I appreciate that this book exists, I don't believe it is something I'll ever revisit.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9744822154489717995" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2982748102" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2982748102" />
    <a title="Ahmad Sharabiani" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/614778-ahmad-sharabiani"><img alt="Ahmad Sharabiani" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1194930432p2/614778.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2982748102?book_show_action=true">Sep 24, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ahmad Sharabiani" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ahmad Sharabiani" href="/user/show/614778-ahmad-sharabiani">Ahmad Sharabiani</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/614778-ahmad-sharabiani?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/614778-ahmad-sharabiani?shelf=21th-century">21th-century</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/614778-ahmad-sharabiani?shelf=mythology">mythology</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/614778-ahmad-sharabiani?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/614778-ahmad-sharabiani?shelf=short-stories">short-stories</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2982748102" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14036731639218803421">Norse Mythology, Neil Gaiman<br/>Norse Mythology is a 2017 book by Neil Gaiman. The book is Gaiman's retelling of several stories from Norse mythology. These stories include the theft of Thor's hammer, the binding of Fenrir and other tales about the Aesir. In Norse Mythology, Gaiman stays true to the myths in envisioning the major Norse pantheon: Odin, the highest of the high, wise, daring, and cunning; Thor, Odin’s son, incredibly strong yet not the wisest of gods; and Loki—son of a giant—blood brot</span>
  <span id="freeText14036731639218803421" style="display:none">Norse Mythology, Neil Gaiman<br />Norse Mythology is a 2017 book by Neil Gaiman. The book is Gaiman's retelling of several stories from Norse mythology. These stories include the theft of Thor's hammer, the binding of Fenrir and other tales about the Aesir. In Norse Mythology, Gaiman stays true to the myths in envisioning the major Norse pantheon: Odin, the highest of the high, wise, daring, and cunning; Thor, Odin’s son, incredibly strong yet not the wisest of gods; and Loki—son of a giant—blood brother to Odin and a trickster and unsurpassable manipulator.<br /><br />عنوانها: اساطیر نورس؛ داستان‌های کهن اسکاندیناوی؛ نویسنده: نیل گیمن؛ تاریخ نخستین خوانش: روز بیست و چهارم ماه ژوئن سال 2019 میلادی<br /><br />عنوان: اساطیر نورس؛ نویسنده: نیل گیمن؛ مترجم: رحیم قاسمیان؛ ویراستار: فرزاد فربد؛ تهران: انتشارات پریان‏‫، ‏‫1397؛ در 288ص؛ شابک 9786007058589؛ ‬‬ موضوع: اساطیر اسکاندیناویایی - سده 21م<br /><br />عنوان: داستان‌های کهن اسکاندیناوی؛ نویسنده: نیل گیمن؛ مترجم: جواد همایون‌پور؛ سبزوار: انتشارات یوبان‏‫، ‏1397؛ در 270ص؛ شابک 9786008349396؛<br />‬<br />کتاب داستانهای کهن اسکاندیناوی، اثری نوشته ی نیل گیمن است که نخستین بار در سال 2017میلادی به چاپ رسید. نیل گیمن که مدتها از اساطیر کهن برای خلق دنیاهای شگفت انگیز داستانهای خود الهام گرفته، در این کتاب به پرداختی نوین از خدایان نورس، و ریشه ها و داستانهای مربوط به آنها دست زده است. گیمن در کتاب داستانهای کهن اسکاندیناوی، با وفاداری و تعهدی ویژه از خدایان چندگانه ی «نورس» سخن میگوید: «اودین، خدای خدایان، خردمند، جسور و زیرک»؛ «ثور، پسر اودین که بی نهایت قدرتمند است اما باهوشترینِ خدایان به حساب نمیآید»؛ و «لوکی، برادر خونی اودین و شخصیتی حیله گر و فوق العاده فرصت طلب». گیمن با نثر جذاب و هیجان انگیز خود به داستانهای افسانه ای این خدایان میپردازد و به آنها، با همه ی پیچیدگیها و ظرافتهای شخصیتیشان، جان دوباره ای میبخشد. اسطوره ­های اسکاندیناوی، اسطوره­ های سرزمین­های سرد هستند، با شب­های زمستانی خیلی خیلی طولانی، و روزهای تابستانی بی ­پایان، اسطوره ­های مردمی که هرگز کاملا به کسی اعتماد نمی­کردند، حتی به ایزدان خودشان، اگرچه از آن­ها می­ترسیدند، و به آن­ها احترام می­گذاشتند. بهترین گمان ما این است که ایزدان آسگارد از آلمان آمدند، و در اسکاندیناوی گسترش یافتند، و بعد به بخش­هایی از جهان، که وایکینگ­ها تصرف کردند، راه یافتند، به جزیره اورکنی اسکاتلند، و سرزمین اسکاتلند، ایرلند و شمال انگلستان، جاییکه این مهاجمان نام «ادین» و «تور» را بر بخش­هایی از آن سرزمین­ها نام­گذاری کردند<br /><br />تاریخ بهنگام رسانی 23/03/1399هجری خورشیدی؛ ا. شربیانی</span>
  <a data-text-id="14036731639218803421" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1839162895" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1839162895" />
    <a title="Markus" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26681101-markus"><img alt="Markus" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1421952301p2/26681101.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1839162895?book_show_action=true">Dec 14, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Markus" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Markus" href="/user/show/26681101-markus">Markus</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780393609097" href="/book/show/30809689-norse-mythology">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26681101-markus?shelf=mythology">mythology</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26681101-markus?shelf=nordic-culture">nordic-culture</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26681101-markus?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26681101-markus?shelf=that-gaiman-guy">that-gaiman-guy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26681101-markus?shelf=2017">2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1839162895" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1588507039936174625"><b>
  <i>"Do you wonder where poetry come from? Where do we get the songs we sing and the tales we tell? Do you ever ask yourself how it is that some people can dream great, wise, beautiful dreams and pass those dreams on as poetry to the world, to be sung and retold as long as the moon will wax and wane? Have you ever wondered why some people make beautiful songs and poems and tales, and some of us do not?<br/>It is a long story, and it does no credit to anyone: there is murder in it, and trickery, lies a</i></b></span>
  <span id="freeText1588507039936174625" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>"Do you wonder where poetry come from? Where do we get the songs we sing and the tales we tell? Do you ever ask yourself how it is that some people can dream great, wise, beautiful dreams and pass those dreams on as poetry to the world, to be sung and retold as long as the moon will wax and wane? Have you ever wondered why some people make beautiful songs and poems and tales, and some of us do not?<br />It is a long story, and it does no credit to anyone: there is murder in it, and trickery, lies and foolishness, seduction and pursuit. Listen."</i>
</b><br /><br />Like Gaiman, I envision these tales being told on long, seemingly everlasting summer nights, and on winter days where the only thing providing light in the darkness is the dancing green shroud of the aurora borealis. Reading his version of the Nordic myths in the family cabin during Yule, surrounded by mountains, fires and snow, was a spectacular experience.<br /><br />As not only a born and bred Scandinavian, but also a historian of Medieval Scandinavia, I am obviously quite familiar with all the stories found among the pages of this little book. That did not mean, however, that I did not adore Gaiman's refreshing, modernised adaptation of them. This book can be read and enjoyed by anyone, from experts to the uniniated.<br /><br />Being obsessed with ancient and Medieval literature often means that I find myself completely uninterested in 'modern' classics. But Gaiman's <i>Norse Mythology</i> merges the old and the new in a truly fascinating manner, and becomes something of a classic in the making, reconciling ancient stories with contemporary methods of writing.<br /><br />Norse mythology is, essentially, the foundation that the modern fantasy genre rests upon. The way this book managed to combine two of my favourite aspects of literature in a single, magical work has turned it into my favourite Neil Gaiman book, as well as one of my favourite books that I've read in recent years.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1588507039936174625" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1796231467" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1796231467" />
    <a title="PorshaJo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5464046-porshajo"><img alt="PorshaJo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1451425289p2/5464046.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1796231467?book_show_action=true">Apr 16, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="PorshaJo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="PorshaJo" href="/user/show/5464046-porshajo">PorshaJo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780393609097" href="/book/show/30809689-norse-mythology">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5464046-porshajo?shelf=challengereads-2017">challengereads-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5464046-porshajo?shelf=challengereads">challengereads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1796231467" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4649129851984394356">I have a confession.....Neil Gaiman is my literary crush (well, one of two) and it in no way influences my feelings for this book. Well, maybe it does. I love everything that he writes and this one is no exception. When I saw he had a new book coming out on Norse Mythology I couldn't wait to get it. <br/><br/>Norse Mythology is a series of stories of myths of the Norse Gods. You learn about Odin, Thor, Loki and many others, how they all came to be. You learn of Asgard, the giants, dwarfs, and more. You he</span>
  <span id="freeText4649129851984394356" style="display:none">I have a confession.....Neil Gaiman is my literary crush (well, one of two) and it in no way influences my feelings for this book. Well, maybe it does. I love everything that he writes and this one is no exception. When I saw he had a new book coming out on Norse Mythology I couldn't wait to get it. <br /><br />Norse Mythology is a series of stories of myths of the Norse Gods. You learn about Odin, Thor, Loki and many others, how they all came to be. You learn of Asgard, the giants, dwarfs, and more. You hear how Thor got his hammer, and then lost it for a very short period of time. You hear so much of the trickster Loki (and who doesn't love Loki). Some stories are quite short and some a bit longer. Some made me see how mean the gods can be and others made me laugh. I have to admit, I have never read a book of Norse mythology so I can't say how this interpretation by Gaiman compares. I thoroughly enjoyed all the stories and savored this one. I immediately started flying through this book as it's so good, but slowed down just to make it last.<br /><br />I had the print version of this, because it arrived first. I ordered both the audio and print. The audio is still in my queue and I plan to listen to this one when it arrives. There is nothing better than having Neil Gaiman read his work. It's almost magical. Yes, yes...I did say he IS my literary crush.<br /><br />Anyway, a great book from Gaiman that gave me some insight into how these tales inspired him in many of his works. Makes me want to go back and re-read American Gods. Granted, this is not my favorite book of his, but a good introduction to Norse mythology. A good book for someone wanting to get started with Gaiman and not exactly sure where to start.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4649129851984394356" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2536260579" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Kayla Dawn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/70522717-kayla-dawn"><img alt="Kayla Dawn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582845179p2/70522717.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2536260579?book_show_action=true">Jul 18, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kayla Dawn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kayla Dawn" href="/user/show/70522717-kayla-dawn">Kayla Dawn</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2536260579" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12964455165548826399">I don't know why but this book failed to keep me interested. It was hard for me to keep focused, I found myself getting distracted really easily.<br/><br/>The writing style was quick and easy and I'm generally very interested in norse mythology, so it doesn't really make sense that I didn't enjoy it that much. But oh well, shit happens lol</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1811215173" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1811215173" />
    <a title="Celeste" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7317186-celeste"><img alt="Celeste" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1481055226p2/7317186.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1811215173?book_show_action=true">Nov 13, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Celeste" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Celeste" href="/user/show/7317186-celeste">Celeste</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780393609097" href="/book/show/30809689-norse-mythology">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7317186-celeste?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7317186-celeste?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7317186-celeste?shelf=non-fiction">non-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1811215173" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16730545719712065493"><b>Full review now posted!</b><br/><br/>When I was a little girl, I was completely obsessed with mythology. Greek, Roman (or Greek with different names, because Rome was nothing if not unoriginal), Norse, Egyptian, Indian, Native American, Japanese, Russian, etc, were all equally interesting to me. I wanted to know what ancient civilizations believed and why, and how those beliefs still influenced their culture. My faith was important to me and heavily influenced how I viewed the world, so why wouldn’t I be inte</span>
  <span id="freeText16730545719712065493" style="display:none"><b>Full review now posted!</b><br /><br />When I was a little girl, I was completely obsessed with mythology. Greek, Roman (or Greek with different names, because Rome was nothing if not unoriginal), Norse, Egyptian, Indian, Native American, Japanese, Russian, etc, were all equally interesting to me. I wanted to know what ancient civilizations believed and why, and how those beliefs still influenced their culture. My faith was important to me and heavily influenced how I viewed the world, so why wouldn’t I be interested in what so heavily influenced other people groups throughout history? As a fourth grader, I was teaching short mythology lessons to junior-high kids before state testing. I loved to learn, and the natural overflow of that love was teaching others. Even then, I always included a segment on Judeo-Christian beliefs, so I could share what I believed as I had shared what ancients believed. I cut my teeth on Edith Hamilton’s <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23522.Mythology_Timeless_Tales_of_Gods_and_Heroes" title="Mythology Timeless Tales of Gods and Heroes by Edith Hamilton" rel="nofollow noopener">Mythology: Timeless Tales of Gods and Heroes</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/588147.Bulfinch_s_Mythology" title="Bulfinch's Mythology by Thomas Bulfinch" rel="nofollow noopener">Bulfinch's Mythology</a>, most of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/20105.Joseph_Campbell" title="Joseph Campbell" rel="nofollow noopener">Joseph Campbell</a>’s mythology books, and more. <br /><br />There was one problem, though. Even though mythology books held incredibly interesting myths, they were generally conveyed like research papers instead of stories. They put forth the tales, but the <i>telling</i> of those tales was generally severely lacking. That was not at all the case with Gaiman’s addition to the mythology genre. He brought in his natural storytelling and breathed new life into the Norse mythos. The book seems small, but writing something of this magnitude was completely outside of his norm, and required more research and tighter restrictions on how that research was interpreted that most novelists ever have to worry about. I respect what he did here immensely, and am excited that now, when a kid develops a love of mythology, they’ll have access to tales well told.<br /><br />The adventures of Odin, Thor, and Loki were a pleasure to read. There were a lot of myths that I had forgotten about or never retained due to the clunky writing of other mythology books. Quite a few of these had me grimacing at one paragraph and laughing at the next. Norse myths are incredibly violent. Their creation myth was the bloodiest creation mythos I ever remember reading. But even in Ragnarok, the end of the world as foretold by the Norsemen, there is hope to be found. <br /><br />I could go into dissecting the stories, but I would hate to spoil anything for someone who is just becoming interested in mythology. But I will say that now I have a burning desire to reread Gaiman’s <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30165203.American_Gods__American_Gods___1_" title="American Gods (American Gods, #1) by Neil Gaiman" rel="nofollow noopener">American Gods</a>. Pick this up if you’ve ever had any kind of interest in ancient beliefs. Just know that this is no novel; this is a faithful retelling of ancient tales, but with style. You’ll learn something if you decide to read this, and you’ll have fun doing it!<br /><br />For more of reviews, as well as my own fiction and thoughts on life, check out my blog, <a>Celestial Musings</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="16730545719712065493" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2543039399" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2543039399" />
    <a title="Leonard Gaya" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27098959-leonard-gaya"><img alt="Leonard Gaya" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442984307p2/27098959.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2543039399?book_show_action=true">Dec 12, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Leonard Gaya" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Leonard Gaya" href="/user/show/27098959-leonard-gaya">Leonard Gaya</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/37756505-norse-mythology">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2543039399" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18254762282874187215">Eight centuries ago, Snorri Sturluson, one of Iceland’s greatest literary glories, wrote the <i>Prose Edda</i>, a significant source for what is left of the ancient religion of the Vikings, with a medieval Christianity twist. Last year, Neil Gaiman, one of Britain’s most celebrated literary glories, wrote this <i>Norse Mythology</i>, a blockbuster retelling of the ancient religion of the Vikings, with a Marvel superhero’s twist.<br/><br/>While it is not always easy to wrap one’s head around Snorri’s prose, Gaiman’s boo</span>
  <span id="freeText18254762282874187215" style="display:none">Eight centuries ago, Snorri Sturluson, one of Iceland’s greatest literary glories, wrote the <i>Prose Edda</i>, a significant source for what is left of the ancient religion of the Vikings, with a medieval Christianity twist. Last year, Neil Gaiman, one of Britain’s most celebrated literary glories, wrote this <i>Norse Mythology</i>, a blockbuster retelling of the ancient religion of the Vikings, with a Marvel superhero’s twist.<br /><br />While it is not always easy to wrap one’s head around Snorri’s prose, Gaiman’s book is delightful and readable, almost a children’s digest of these arcane myths of pre-Christian Scandinavia. The colourful tales flow naturally under Gaiman’s pen as if they were a collection of Grimm’s fairytales or Lancelyn Green’s recounting of the Arthurian legends.<br /><br />Gaiman addresses the reader as if he were a skald speaking to an audience gathered around a campfire under chilly stars. He starts off with the dismemberment of the cosmic Ymir at the beginning of times, and leads us through the various adventures of the gods of Asgard, in particular Odin, Thor and Loki, against different kinds of cave-dwarfs and frost-giants, all the way to the last battle of Ragnarök, at the end of days. I particularly love the stories that involve this most unlikely duo, the coarse and invincible Thor and the devious and shapeshifting Loki. Some of their adventures, for instance their encounter with the Brobdingnagian Skrymir/Utgardaloki, are fascinating; others, like Thor’s wedding with the ogre Thrym, are priceless. Gaiman’s description of Ragnarök is both sublime and sinister: indubitably the best section of the whole book.<br /><br />However, while Snorri Sturluson went on to tell the stories of the hero Sigurd, Gaiman restricts himself to the narratives concerning the gods. Therefore, you will not find a word in his book about the heroic Norsemen — historical or legendary — who are mentioned in Snorri’s <i>Heimskringla</i>, in Saxo’s <i>Gesta Danorum</i> (the source of Shakespeare’s <i>Hamlet</i>), in the <i>Völsunga Saga</i>, or the <i>Nibelungenlied</i>.<br /><br />Naturally, these myths, which had been stifled under Christian domination, resurfaced in the 19th century with Richard Wagner’s <i>Ring des Nibelungen</i>, and in the 20th century with J. R. R. Tolkien — the <i>Silmarillion</i> is a fascinating variation on the Norse myths. More recently, G. R. R. Martin borrowed quite a few themes from these old myths in his <i>Song of Ice and Fire</i>, and there are now literally piles of YA novels that giddily, and maybe unwittingly, loot and misrepresent Snorri’s legacy. Gaiman’s book, however, is an honest, faithful, engaging and robust endeavour to make it shine yet again.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18254762282874187215" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1838009583" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('7X33xl6sQcPsCY9HJoGnnE+PPjzejg/lnxFLMyIEMZPXW54U5fKIq0siOybRdK1DmdDZ9BADgYLEbw2C70fDCQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('KqLSNwSOna8wAVdHBzVIu1TJATBLgWxsuqW8IyRdWyYQhLvlv9BUx5cq4ybwwEJkgpbm+IUM4gvh2/qS6R6pvA==')})
  }
